## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor rate laws / ODE kinetics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the canonical form for kinetic rate laws in chemistry (rate expressions defining an ODE in time). With only (t, A) available, common models include order-based power-law kinetics, reversible/relaxation-to-equilibrium forms, autocatalysis, and time-varying (deactivating) rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant net generation/consumption; e.g., surface-limited or constant feed/removal)
- Zero-order decay with sign constraint: dA_dt = -c0 (constant consumption in batch when reactant is in large excess elsewhere)
- First-order (unimolecular) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition, many pseudo-first-order cases)
- General n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate law when order is unknown)
- Second-order (bimolecular/self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (2A -> products or A+B with B absorbed into c0 under pseudo-steady conditions)
- Mixed source + first-order sink: dA_dt = c0 + -c1 * A (inflow/formation plus first-order removal; linear kinetics around a baseline)
- Approach-to-equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A + -c1) (drives A toward equilibrium level A_eq = c1; common linearization of reversible kinetics)
- Reversible-like with forward/backward lumped in A (quadratic relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (net rate from competing forward/backward channels approximated in a single-state model)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-type consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + -A) (sigmoidal time course in batch via self-acceleration then depletion; c1 is a capacity/maximum level)
- Inhibition/saturation in the rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to site limitation or self-inhibition phenomenology)
- Catalyst deactivation / time-varying rate coefficient (exponential): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective first-order with activity decaying in time)
- Time-ramped kinetics (power-law in time): dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A (induction/activation effects captured by a time-dependent prefactor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ÔåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ÔåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ÔåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ÔåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ÔåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production: negative dA_dt typically indicates reactant depletion; models often enforce dA_dt <= 0 for A >= 0 via a leading minus sign on positive-prefactor terms.
- Reaction order identification: proportionality dA_dt ÔêØ A implies first-order; ÔêØ A**2 implies second-order; ÔêØ A**n (non-integer n) suggests empirical/global kinetics or transport-affected kinetics.
- Equilibrium/relaxation behavior: a factor (A + -c1) indicates attraction to a steady concentration A_eq = c1 (effective reversible kinetics or chemostat-like relaxation).
- Autocatalysis signature: a product form A*(c1 + -A) (or similar) produces slow start, acceleration, then slowdown as A approaches a limiting levelÔÇötypical of self-catalyzed pathways or constrained capacity.
- Catalyst/activity decay: multiplying a base rate term by exp(-c*t) indicates time-dependent loss of activity (deactivation, fouling) independent of A except through the base kinetics.
- Induction/activation periods: shifting time as (t + c1) and raising to a power can emulate delayed onset or gradual activation without introducing extra state variables.
- Linear source-plus-sink: c0 + -c1*A implies a stable steady state A* = c0/c1 (in physical terms: balance between constant formation and proportional removal).
- Stiff depletion near zero: high powers A**c1 with c1 > 1 tend to slow consumption dramatically at low A, producing long tails in A(t).
- Finite-time blow-down avoidance: forms like -c*A (vs -c) naturally prevent A from going negative in continuous-time solutions (exponential vs linear decline).
